                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Materials for Chemical Capacitive Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhai, Yunpu; Dou, Yuqian; Zhao, Dongyuan; Fulvio, Pasquale F.; Mayes, Richard T.; Dai, Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Carbon materials have attracted intense interests as electrode materials for electrochem. capacitors, because of their high surface area, elec. cond., chem. stability and low cost.  Activated carbons produced by different activation processes from various precursors are the most widely used electrodes.  Recently, with the rapid growth of nanotechnol., nanostructured electrode materials, such as carbon nanotubes and template-synthesized porous carbons have been developed.  Their unique elec. properties and well controlled pore sizes and structures facilitate fast ion and electron transportation.  In order to further improve the power and energy densities of the capacitors, carbon-based composites combining elec. double layer capacitors (EDLC)-capacitance and pseudo-capacitance have been explored.  They show not only enhanced capacitance, but as well good cyclability.  Recent progress on carbon-based electrode materials is summarized, including activated carbons, carbon nanotubes, and template-synthesized porous carbons, in particular mesoporous carbons.  Their advantages and disadvantages as electrochem. capacitors are discussed.  The future trends of electrochem. capacitors with high energy and power are proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbtLKCSuKRLLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZcN8K1FRYnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1Wrs7jE&amp;md5=90635c29d366318b663e22827b54f043</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12538"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">She, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Natural Lignin: A Sustainable and Cost-Effective Electrode Material for High-Temperature Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Petroleum asphaltene-derived highly porous carbon for efficient removal of pharmaceutical compounds in water</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kabatas, Melike Burcu; Cetinkaya, Sevil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Porous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly porous carbons (PCs) were successfully developed through KOH chem. activation process from petroleum asphaltene for the efficient removal of pharmaceutical compds. (paracetamol and salicylic acid) from aq. soln.  The influences of activation temp. and the mixing types in chem. activation on the properties of the resulting PCs were investigated in detail by SEM, XRD, TGA, Raman, nitrogen adsorption-desorption, and CHNS elemental analyses.  The PC with an extremely high surface area (2470 m2/g) was obtained by the impregnation method without modifier at an activation temp. of 850°C.  Adsorption kinetics was investigated with three kinetic models called the pseudo-first-order, the pseudo-second-order, and the intra-particle diffusion models, besides the adsorption equil. was analyzed using three widely used isotherm equations (Langmuir, Freundlich, and Temkin).  The pseudo-second-order model was the best compatible with the exptl. data for both org. compds.  This PC exhibited a high paracetamol adsorption capacity of 476.2 mg/g and a salicylic adsorption capacity of 500.0 mg/g in water.  Thermodn. analyzes confirmed that the adsorption was an exothermic process (ΔH0 = - 18.63 kJ/mol) for paracetamol and an endothermic process (ΔH0 = 53.96 kJ/mol) for salicylic acid.  The linearized Freundlich and Langmuir models fitted the equil. data better than the others for paracetamol and salicylic acid, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqN-Wuz5xC2PrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZcN8K1FRYnQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous carbon nanosheet derived from waste engine oil for high-performance supercapacitor application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yubing; Zhang, Deyi; He, Jingjing; Wang, Yulin; Zhang, Xiai; Zhang, Yameng; Liu, Xuexin; Wang, Kunjie; Wang, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Energy &amp; Fuels</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of electrode materials with high-performance and low-cost is crucial for the development of electrochem. energy storage devices.  Waste engine oil is a toxic and hazardous waste; it is estd. that about 45 million tons of waste engine oil are generated per yr worldwide.  Herein, waste engine oil was first recycled as a raw material to fabricate hierarchical porous carbon nanosheets.  The obtained material exhibited high sp. surface area (up to 2276 m2 g-1), hierarchical porous structure, and excellent capacitance performance.  Its specific capacitance reached 352 F g-1, and more than 87.7% of initial capacitance was retained when the c.d. was increased from 0.5 to 20 A g-1.  In addn., no apparent capacitance drop was obsd. after 5000 charge and discharge cycles.  The superior capacitance performance than that of the com. activated carbon and most of the waste-derived porous carbons, cheap and readily available raw materials, and environmental benefit due to proper recycling of the hazardous waste make the reported hierarchical porous carbon nanosheet a promising energy storage material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrc-KAw_C5XO7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZcN8K1FRYnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFWisL7P&amp;md5=4690065540d8ec67130cba2fb9a97be3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijbiomac.2022.08.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muddasar, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Beaucamp, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Culebras, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, M.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cellulose: Characteristics and applications for rechargeable batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Muddasar, Muhammad; Beaucamp, A.; Culebras, Mario; Collins, Maurice N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Biological Macromolecules</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Cellulose, an abundant natural polymer, has promising potential to be used for energy storage systems because of its excellent mech., structural, and phys. characteristics.  This review discusses the structural features of cellulose and describes its potential application as an electrode, separator, and binder, in various types of high-performing batteries.  Various surface and structural characteristics of cellulose (e.g., fiber size, surface functional groups, the hierarchy of pores, and porosity levels) that contribute to its electrochem. performance are discussed.  Cellulose structure/property/processing/function relationships are further focused and elucidated in terms of the latest developments in the emerging field of sustainable materials in Li-Ion, Na-Ion, and Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiDC0Cj1kQUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1gdju6F41fw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitFalu7jL&amp;md5=6dfa683b617e929ec5393a44d8141eaf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.pnsc.2022.09.004"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Khajonrit, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sichumsaeng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kalawa, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chaisit, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chinnakorn, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chanlek, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maensiri, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mangosteen peel-derived activated carbon for supercapacitors</span>. <i>Prog.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mangosteen peel-derived activated carbon for supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Khajonrit, Jessada; Sichumsaeng, Thongsuk; Kalawa, Ornuma; Chaisit, Suphawi; Chinnakorn, Atchara; Chanlek, Narong; Maensiri, Santi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Progress in Natural Science: Materials International</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports the effects of activation temps. on the porous development and electrochem. performance of activated carbons.  Herein, activated carbons were prepd. from the biowaste of mangosteen peel by using KOH activation at temps. of 400, 600, and 800°C.  The results demonstrate that the sp. surface area increases with increasing the activation temps. in which the well-developed porous structure after KOH activation at 800°C provides the highest sp. surface area of 1039 m2 g-1.  At 600°C, the activated carbon delivers the highest specific capacitance value of 182 F g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 in 3 M KOH aq. electrolyte.  This is correlated well with its high micropore fractions (99%).  Moreover, it was found that the activation temp. changes the major contribution of oxygen-contg. functional group on surface of activated carbon, which is beneficial for the enhancement of the specific capacitance value of activated carbon at the temp. of 600°C.  This work suggests that the activation temp. is a key to optimizing the electrochem. performance of activated carbons.  Overall, our activated carbons can be considered as a strong candidate for use as electrode materials in supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqVhtnf-BNWBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1gdju6F41fw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xis1aiurfM&amp;md5=8852d7a47dec4633b5760de938075092</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.materresbull.2021.111281"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bamboo-derived porous carbons for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span>. <i>Mater.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bamboo-derived porous carbons for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hao; Zheng, Yu; Zhu, Xinqiang; Hong, Wenliang; Tong, Yifei; Lu, Yingzhuo; Pei, Gu; Pang, Yajun; Shen, Zhehong; Guan, Cao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Research Bulletin</span>

                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crosslinking and self-assembly synthesis of tannin-based carbon frameworks cathode for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Shuxin; Wei, Qinhong; Fan, Huailin; Zhang, Yuanrong; Gao, Guoming; Hu, Xun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">644</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">478-486</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon frameworks with well-developed porosity present broad application prospects in energy-related materials, and green prepn. still face challenges.  Herein, the tannins-derived framework-like carbon material is obtained by crosslinking and self-assembly strategy.  The phenolic hydroxyl and quinones in tannin crosslinking react with the amine groups in the methenamine by simple stirring, which drives the self-assembly of tannins and methenamine, contributing to the reaction products being pptd. in soln. as aggregates with framework-like structure.  The porosity and micromorphol. of framework-like structures are further enriched by the thermal stability difference between tannin and methenamine.  The methenamine of framework-like structures is entirely removed by the sublimation and decompn. and the tannin is transformed into carbon materials inheriting framework-like structures after the carbonization, which offers the path for rapid electron transport.  The framework-like structure, excellent sp. surface area and nitrogen doping give the assembled Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors a superior specific capacitance of 165.3 mAh·g-1 (350.4 F·g-1).  This device could be charged to 1.87 V to power the bulb by using solar panels.  This study proves that the tannin-derived framework-like carbon is a promising electrode of the Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors, which is beneficial for value-added and industrial supercapacitors application of green feedstocks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPv9X1LPo4PrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1gdju6F41fw"> &gt;&gt; Here, an N, O co-doped two-dimensional (2D) carbon nanosheet material is successfully fabricated via a one-step combustion conversion of wood for the excellent usage as the cathode material in zinc-ion hybrid supercapacitors.  This novel combustion conversion synthesis with Zn(NO3)2·6H2O as oxidizer and urea as fuel can easily achieve the carbonization, pore-forming, and heteroatom doping within a one-step process.  More interestingly, the resulting N, O co-doped porous carbon owns relatively uniform 2D sheet structure and very high sp. surface area (1248 m2 g-1), which can not only provide short elec./ionic transfer path plus optimized wettability and cond. for high power output, but also offer abundant interfacial active sites as well as improved ion adsorption capacity for high energy storage.  Benefiting from these advantages, the ZHS based on this N, O co-doped 2D carbon nanosheets exhibits a superior specific capacity of 111.0 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, high rate capability of 57.6% capacity retention at a 30-fold higher current, and attractive energy d. of 109.5 Wh kg-1 at 225 W kg-1.  More gratifyingly, it displays ultralong cycling life with 92.7% capacity reservation after 50,000 charge and discharge cycles.  Moreover, a quasi-solid ZHS with N, O co-doped 2D carbon nanosheets coated on the carbon cloth as the cathode also displays satisfactory specific capacity (34.6 mAh g-1), impressive energy d. (27.7 Wh kg-1), and nice flexibility.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFItdrbJNRErVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1gdju6F41fw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1ekur3F&amp;md5=6fca247c3e0177f072a6dce23a2f6db0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/B978-0-12-823702-1.00011-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, M.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thermoelectric properties of electrospun carbon nanofibres derived from lignin</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dalton, Niall; Lynch, Robert P.; Collins, Maurice N.; Culebras, Mario</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Biological Macromolecules</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing sustainable and efficient thermoelec. materials is a challenge because the most common thermoelec. materials are based on rare elements such as bismuth and telluride.  In this context, we have produced bio-based carbon nanofibres (CNFs) derived from mixts. of polyacrylonitrile and lignin using electrospinning.  The addn. of lignin (up to 70%) reduces the diam. of CNFs from 450 nm to 250 nm, increases sample flexibility, and promotes inter-fiber fusion.  The cryst. structure of the CNFs was analyzed by Raman spectroscopy.  The elec. cond. and the Seebeck coeff. were evaluated as function of the lignin content in the precursor and carbonised equiv.  Finally, a conversion of p-type to n-type semiconducting behavior was achieved with a hydrazine vapor treatment.  We observe a max. p-type power factor of 9.27μW cm-1 K-2 for CNFs carbonised at 900°C with 70% lignin which is a 34.5-fold increase to the CNFs with 0% lignin.  For the hydrazine treated samples, we observe a max. n-type power factor of 10.2μW cm-1 K-2 for the CNFs produced in the same way which is an 11.0-fold increase to the hydrazine-treated CNFs with 0% lignin.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrH6fN14ezFY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEyusBXtbVFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFChurfM&amp;md5=ead8d2e33839be5a81e21154f6534d26</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202100896"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef, H.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lignin Derived Porous Carbons: Synthesis Methods and Supercapacitor Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenli; Yin, Jian; Wang, Caiwei; Zhao, Lei; Jian, Wenbin; Lu, Ke; Lin, Haibo; Qiu, Xueqing; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lignin, one of the renewable constituents in natural plant biomasses, holds great potential as a sustainable source of functional carbon materials.  Tremendous research efforts have been made on lignin-derived carbon electrodes for rechargeable batteries.  However, lignin is considered as one of the most promising carbon precursors for the development of high-performance, low-cost porous carbon electrode materials for supercapacitor applications.  Yet, these efforts have not been reviewed in detail in the current literature.  This review, therefore, offers a basis for the utilization of lignin as a pivotal precursor for the synthesis of porous carbons for use in supercapacitor electrode applications.  Lignin chem., the synthesis process of lignin-derived porous carbons, and future directions for developing better porous carbon electrode materials from lignin are systematically reviewed.  Technol. hurdles and approaches that should be prioritized in future research are presented.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoUd4Y_Q2AVRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEyusBXtbVFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xkt1Wjtbs%253D&amp;md5=119cf91b1a6c7ed175ead8978c6caa4e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.30919/es8d608"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Culebras, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, G. Lignin is the most abundant arom. biopolymer on the planet with its chem. structure rendering it ideal for carbon materials prodn. and finely tailored architectures of these sustainable carbon materials are beginning to find use in high value energy applications.  This review focuses on lignin chem., various lignin extn. and fractionation techniques, and their impact on lignin structure/property relationships for energy applications are discussed.  Chemistries behind important and emerging energy applications from recent research on this increasingly valuable sustainable polymer are described.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsjiZiviK6K7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEyusBXtbVFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xis1WgurnE&amp;md5=80056d0ef3deeaf64e8e4ed92e660ba5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/bbb.2083"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ragauskas, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lignin-derived electrochemical energy materials and systems</span>. <i>Biofuels, Bioprod.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lignin-derived electrochemical energy materials and systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xiaoyu; Jiang, Junhua; Wang, Chongmin; Liu, Jian; Pu, Yunqiao; Ragauskas, Arthur; Li, Songmei; Yang, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Biofuels, Bioproducts &amp; Biorefining</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrode and electrolyte materials with higher performance, longer life, and lower cost need to be developed, given the substantial growing demand for advanced electrochem. energy systems.  Lignin, the second most abundant natural polymer, has been successfully demonstrated to be a viable precursor or feedstock for the prepn. of high-performance electrochem. energy materials and components such as electrodes, electrolyte additives, membrane separators, and binders.  Moreover, techno-economic analyses indicate that it is possible to prep. cost-effective carbon structures from lignin at engineering scale, in contrast with current carbon products.  These facts suggest that the scalable conversion of lignin into high-value energy materials will offer a promising pathway to not only promote the utilization and valorization of lignin but also boost the development of advanced electrochem. energy systems.  This review examines cutting-edge renewable energy materials derived from various lignin compds. and their applications in electrochem. energy systems with an emphasis on supercapacitors, rechargeable batteries, and fuel cells.  Meanwhile, this review also aims to carve out the crit. barriers for lignin-derived high-performance materials for energy applications, and to identify viable approaches for the synthesis of sustainable new energy materials. © 2020 Society of Chem.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Valorization of biodigestor plant waste in electrodes for supercapacitors and microbial fuel cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mutuma, Bridget K.; Sylla, Ndeye F.; Bubu, Amanda; Ndiaye, Ndeye M.; Santoro, Carlo; Brilloni, Alessandro; Poli, Federico; Manyala, Ncholu; Soavi, Francesca</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">391</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This study aims at demonstrating that wastes from anaerobic biodigester plants can be effectively valorized as functional materials to be implemented in technologies that enable efficient energy management and water treatment, therefore simultaneously addressing the Water-Energy-Waste Nexus challenges.  Lignin, the main solid residue of the biodigester plant, has been valorized into activated biochar with a mild activation agent, like KHCO3, to produce electrode of supercapacitors and microbial fuel cells.  In addn., the same sludge that is the liq. effluent of the biodigester plant has been exploited as inoculum and electrolyte for the MFC.  The lignin-derived carbons obtained at lignin/KHCO3 mass ratios of 1:0.5 (LAC-0.5) and 1:2 (LAC-2) comprised of mesopores and micropores displaying BETs of 1558 m2g-1 and 1879 m2g-1, resp.  LAC-2 carbon exhibited a superior specific capacitance of 114 F g-1 in 2.5 M KNO3 with respect to LAC-0.5.  A supercapacitor with LAC-2 electrodes was built displaying specific energy specific power up to 10 Wh kg-1 and 6.9 kW kg-1, resp.  Durability tests showed that the device was able to maintain a capacitance retention of 84.5% after 15,000 charge-discharge cycles.  The lignin-derived carbons were also studied as electrocatalysts for ORR in a neutral medium.  The LAC-2 showed higher ORR electrocatalytic activity than LAC-0.5.  The interconnected porous network and the high surface area made the lignin-derived porous carbons suitable electrode materials for dual applications.  The feasibility of the use of LAC 2 carbon incorporated in an air breathing cathode for MFC applications is also reported.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDvzWmLCPef7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslWltLbJ&amp;md5=242e1d507b8fbdc0a7b8ec848a47ea49</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijbiomac.2022.09.097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Beaucamp, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muddasar, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Crawford, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, M.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sustainable lignin precursors for tailored porous carbon-based supercapacitor electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Beaucamp, Anne; Muddasar, Muhammad; Crawford, Tara; Collins, Maurice N.; Culebras, Mario</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Biological Macromolecules</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sustainable materials are attracting a lot of attention since they will be crit. in the creation of the next generation of products and devices.  In this study, hydrogels were effectively synthesized utilizing lignin, a non-valorised biopolymer from the paper industry.  This study proposes a method based on utilizing lignin to create highly swollen hydrogels using poly(ethylene) glycol diglycidyl ether (PEGDGE) as a crosslinking agent.  The influence of different crosslinker ratios on the structural and chem. properties of the resultant hydrogels was investigated.  Pore size was obsd. to be lowered when the amt. of crosslinker was increased.  The inclusion of addnl. hydrophilic groups in the hydrogel network decreased the swelling capacity of the hydrogels as the crosslinking d. increases.  These precursor materials were carbonised and electrochem. tested for application as electrodes for supercapacitors with capacitance characterized as a function of crosslinker ratio.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPzj0rQp2RELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVSntL3I&amp;md5=62fa0200c24f87e7828ceee309974020</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsanm.2c01033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thomas, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lycksam, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sain, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oksman, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ice-Templating of Lignin and Cellulose Nanofiber-Based Carbon Aerogels: Implications for Energy Storage Applications</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ice-Templating of Lignin and Cellulose Nanofiber-Based Carbon Aerogels: Implications for Energy Storage Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thomas, Bony; Geng, Shiyu; Wei, Jiayuan; Lycksam, Henrik; Sain, Mohini; Oksman, Kristiina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Nano Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7954-7966</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchically porous carbon aerogels (CAs) were synthesized by following a green, facile prepn. route involving ice-templating and lyophilization followed by carbonization.  For the first time, we report CAs prepd. with a cooling rate of 7.5 K/min, demonstrating a very high sp. surface area (SSA) of 1260 m2 g-1 without any phys. or chem. activation steps, and the electrode prepd. using the latter aerogel showed superior electrochem. performance with a specific capacitance of 410 F g-1 at 2 m V s-1 with a cyclic stability of 94% after 4500 charge-discharge cycles.  The effects of the ice-templating cooling rate and the solid content of lignin and cellulose nanofibers (CNFs) in the suspension on the structure and electrochem. performance of the CAs were investigated.  The ice-templating process and the cooling rate were found to have a large effect on the generation of the nanoporous structure and the sp. surface area of carbon aerogels, while the solid content of the lignin-nanocellulose suspension showed negligible effects.  When assembled as a supercapacitor (SC), a remarkable specific capacitance of 240 F g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 was achieved.  The relaxation time const. for the prepd. SC was 1.3 s, which shows the fast response of these SCs.  In addn., an energy d. of 4.3 Wh kg-1 was also obtained at a power d. of 500 W kg-1.  Thus, this study opens new perspectives for the prepn. of green, environment-friendly, free-standing, high-performance CA electrodes for future energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCBc37HZQFkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtlKjs7%252FP&amp;md5=ea85df1bfc3f7f1032d4df860411d70c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1007/s10854-021-05410-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Template-free synthesis of lignin-derived 3D hierarchical porous carbon for supercapacitors</span>. <i>J.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7009-7018</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSMEEV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0957-4522</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile synthesis strategy for lignin-derived three-dimensional hierarchical porous carbon (LHPC) was developed in this work.  The LHPC was synthesized by a one-step carbonization-activation process using lignin as a carbon precursor and wet KOH as an in situ chem. activation agent.  Compared with dry KOH activation agent, the wet KOH shows exfoliation effect on assisting the formation of hierarchical porous structure of LHPC.  The H2O plays a key role of an exfoliation agent in forming the hierarchical porous structure of LHPC.  The as-prepd. LHPC shows a high sp. surface area of 2109 m2 g-1 and hierarchical pores.  When used as an electrode material for supercapacitor, the LHPC exhibits excellent electrochem. performances, including a high capacitance of 254 F g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 and excellent rate capability with 59% capacitance retention at 20 A g-1.  This study offers a convenient and practical approach to produce a high-rate hierarchical porous carbon material for supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvajy__RpUorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktlansbo%253D&amp;md5=4ecd54e7391de3e27158fe9d9cb29591</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C8GC01577E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Culebras, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanchis, M.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the thermal and dielectric response of organosolv and modified kraft lignin as a carbon fibre precursor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Culebras, Mario; Sanchis, Maria J.; Beaucamp, Anne; Carsi, Marta; Kandola, Baljinder K.; Horrocks, A. Richard; Panzetti, Gianmarco; Birkinshaw, Colin; Collins, Maurice N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Green Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Understanding the thermal behavior of lignin is crucial to realize its valorization as an engineering polymer.  Two hardwood lignins, organosolv (OSL) and chem. modified kraft lignin (ML) were chosen to represent important classes of renewable and abundant raw materials.  The relation between ionic mobility and viscosity in OSL and ML was studied.  The rheol. results were interpreted in terms of the competitive processes of thermal plasticization and stiffening through crosslinking.  Results show that with OSL, crosslinking proceeds relatively rapidly, and this is consistent with its more reactive structure.  Higher mol. wt. (Mw) influenced the melt stability as crosslinking kinetics was reduced and this was attributed to the redn. of chain ends available for crosslinking reactions.  Scanning calorimetry has shown that both materials are glassy and pass through the glass transition between 100 °C and 115 °C, with the higher mol. wt. modified material having a slightly higher Tg.  Both lignins show pronounced maxima in the Gram-Schmidt plots for methane or methanol around 400 °C.  However, a significant difference between the materials is obsd. with the detection of a strong carbonyl peak in the evolution products of the ML, which is attributed to the scission of the hydroxypropyl substituent present in the ML structure.  The differences in the degrdn. processes are further reflected in the dielec. properties of the partially degraded materials where loss maxima occur at different temps. and show different degrees of frequency dependence.  An important observation is the difference in cond., where higher values for OSL are attributed to the crosslinking between adjacent benzene rings, whereas with the ML, a lower cond. is assocd. with intrinsically less conductive intermol. linkages.  These results demonstrate that the thermal decompn. of the two lignins follows significantly different paths at the mol. level.  With the more reactive OSL, it appears to be the case that there is a greater tendency to form direct ring to ring crosslinks and this is significant for the properties of the intended end product.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq3ub32NUTw4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlajsbrI&amp;md5=f5f8e66e7cc1de8b4190bec0844c5e89</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201907176"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hanaor, D.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freeze Casting: From Low-Dimensional Building Blocks to Aligned Porous Structures-A Review of Novel Materials, Methods, and Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Gaofeng; Hanaor, Dorian A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Freeze casting, also known as ice templating, is a particularly versatile technique that has been applied extensively for the fabrication of well-controlled biomimetic porous materials based on ceramics, metals, polymers, biomacromols., and carbon nanomaterials, endowing them with novel properties and broadening their applicability.  The principles of different directional freeze-casting processes are described and the relationships between processing and structure are examd.  Recent progress in freeze-casting assisted assembly of low dimensional building blocks, including graphene and carbon nanotubes, into tailored micro- and macrostructures is then summarized.  Emerging trends relating to novel materials as building blocks and novel freeze-cast geometries-beads, fibers, films, complex macrostructures, and nacre-mimetic composites-are presented.  Thereafter, the means by which aligned porous structures and nacre mimetic materials obtainable through recently developed freeze-casting techniques and low-dimensional building blocks can facilitate material functionality across multiple fields of application, including energy storage and conversion, environmental remediation, thermal management, and smart materials, are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6lM6FlhbE-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgepWQQDnWemw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXkvFanuro%253D&amp;md5=797661fe6a01c770337ccd22cdd3ba7c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.powtec.2018.09.038"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pérez-Rodríguez, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Torres, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lázaro, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports a study of the elec. cond. under compression of nanostructured carbon powders with different physicochem. properties (texture, chem.-surface and morphol.): a com. carbon black (Vulcan XC-72R) and synthesized ordered mesoporous carbon (OMC), carbon nanocoils (CNC) and carbon nanofibers (CNF).         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance and low-cost electrochem. capacitors (ECs) are essential for large-scale applications in energy storage.  In this work, the specific capacitance of active carbon (AC) electrode was significantly improved through the combination of introducing functional groups on the surface of AC and adding redox-active mols. (K3Fe(CN)6) into 2 M KOH aq. electrolytes.  The surface-oxygen functionalized AC (FAC) was synthesized using HNO3 echoed as the electrode and 2 M KOH with 0.1 M K3Fe(CN)6 as the electrolyte.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting electrochemical properties of carbon materials as bipolar electrodes by introducing oxygen functional groups</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yaxiong; Liu, Ying; Bai, Yunfei; Liu, Yupeng; Xie, Erqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon materials are often used as both pos. and neg. electrodes (bipolar electrode materials) in energy storage devices, which significantly reduces the prepn. complexity of the electrode.  Herein, oxygen-modified carbon nanotubes mounted on carbon cloth (CCC) present a high areal capacitance as both pos. and neg. electrodes in a safe neutral electrolyte.  The introduction of oxygen functional groups facilitates the formation of many electrochem. active sites and defects conducive to ion diffusion.  When carbon materials are utilized as neg. electrodes, the charge storage characteristics are mainly dependent on the adsorption and desorption of the ions (corresponding to the elec. double layer capacitance).  Whereas, when utilized as pos. electrodes, the charge storage characteristics come from the intercalation and de-intercalation of the electrolyte ions in the multi-defect carbon material.  The max. areal capacitance measured at the pos. electrode and neg. electrode was 336 mF cm-2 and 158 mF cm-2, resp.  The measured areal capacitance of the assembled sym. supercapacitors was 93.6 mF cm-2, and the areal energy d. reached 33μW h cm-2 at a power d. of 793μW cm-2.  It is believed that the efficient prepn. method and electrochem. mechanism elucidated in this work can guide the practical applications of carbon cloth in supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPcu92gGELZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liKLJ1CKtT91A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFajtrjE&amp;md5=742490022338f3cff76efacab996adfb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201901562"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Culebras, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geaney, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Beaucamp, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Upadhyaya, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dalton, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryan, K.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bio-derived Carbon Nanofibres from Lignin as High-Performance Li-Ion Anode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Culebras, Mario; Geaney, Hugh; Beaucamp, Anne; Upadhyaya, Prathviraj; Dalton, Eric; Ryan, Kevin M.; Collins, Maurice N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

Herein, the prepn. of carbon nanofibres from biopolymer blends of lignin (byproduct from the paper and pulp industry) and polylactic acid (PLA) or a thermoplastic elastomeric polyurethane (TPU) is described.  SEM anal. shows the evolving microstructural morphol. after each processing step (electrospinning, stabilization and carbonisation).                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct one-pot synthesis of ordered mesoporous carbons from lignin with metal coordinated self-assembly</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiaoqi; Liu, Xiaoning; Smith, Richard Lee; Liang, Yining; Qi, Xinhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Green Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Conventional soft template methods for the synthesis of ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs) use unsustainable, toxic and carcinogenic phenolic compds. as carbon precursors and aldehydes as crosslinkers.  Lignin is a potential carbon precursor for OMC prodn., but its direct use as a carbon precursor has not been possible.  Herein, a protocol is developed for the direct one-pot synthesis of OMCs using lignin from agricultural waste sources (walnut shell, macadamia nut shell, and tobacco stem) as a sole carbon precursor through coordinated interactions between lignin functional groups and metal ligands via classical solvent evapn. induced self-assembly (EISA).  The protocol is demonstrated for the one-pot synthesis of metal oxide- or elemental metal-linked OMCs (defined as M#OMCs) using many different metal ions (Ni2+, Mg2+, Fe3+, Co2+, Zn2+, La3+, and Ce3+) that form well-ordered mesoporous structures having uniform metal dispersion.  As one application, Ni#OMC is shown to effectively catalyze biomass hydrogenation, transfer hydrogenation and isomerization reactions.  The protocol developed for OMC materials from lignin is expected to have wide applications in catalysis, adsorption, sensor, drug delivery and energy storage fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohJbWsKtNIZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7hoEVOGsRiQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The O-N-S co-doped hierarchical porous carbons are prepd. by direct pyrolysis of kraft lignin which is the byproduct from papermaking black liquor.  The proposed prepn. method is extremely facile, green-environmentally, and low-cost without any addnl. activating agents, additives, or templates.  The kraft lignin-derived carbon materials possess large sp. surface areas (338-1307 m2 g-1), hierarchical porous structures and abundant multi-heteroatoms co-doping (9.84-19.91 wt%).  Benefiting from above synergistic advantages, the as-fabricated sym. supercapacitor in aq. electrolyte delivers a high specific capacitance of 244.5 F g-1 at 0.2 A g-1, excellent rate-capability (81.8% retention of initial capacitance at 40.0 A g-1), and outstanding cycling stability (91.6% retention over 10000 cycles).  Importantly, this device in aq. electrolyte delivers an energy d. of 8.5 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 100 W kg-1.  Furthermore, a remarkable energy d. of 66.8 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 1.75 kW kg-1 has been achieved and 32.2 W h kg-1 is still maintained even at an ultrahigh power d. of 40.0 kW kg-1 when ionic liq. serves as electrolyte.  This study demonstrates the successful conversion of low-valued natural biomass deriv. into sustainable high-performance supercapacitor electrode materials with a simple, low-cost, and green-environmental prodn. process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPIfidJJTaZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7hoEVOGsRiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXnvV2ltrk%253D&amp;md5=71151eebe61e8e36b0bc5a60daabf26a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1038/s41598-020-64020-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coal-based 3D hierarchical porous carbon aerogels for high performance and super-long life supercapacitors</span>. <i>Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: Coal-based 3D hierarchical porous carbon aerogels (3D HPCAs) has been successfully fabricated from a freeze-drying method and with subsequent of calcination process, using coal oxide as carbon precursors, and PVA as both crosslinking agent and sacrifice template.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Methods for preparation and activation of activated carbon: a review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Heidarinejad, Zoha; Dehghani, Mohammad Hadi; Heidari, Mohsen; Javedan, Gholamali; Ali, Imran; Sillanpaa, Mika</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Environmental Chemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Activated carbon refers to a wide range of carbonised materials of high degree of porosity and high surface area.  Activated carbon has many applications in the environment and industry for the removal, retrieval, sepn. and modification of various compds. in liq. and gas phases.  Selection of the chem. activator agent is a major step controlling the performance and applicability of activated carbon.  Here, we review chem. activators used to produce activated carbon.  We compare the impregnation method with the phys. mixing method used in activating with alkali hydroxides.  We selected 81 articles from Google Scholar, PubMed, Scopus, Science Direct, Embase and Medlin databases.  Eighteen articles report the activation with potassium hydroxide, 17 with phosphoric acid, 15 with zinc chloride, 11 with potassium carbonate, nine with sodium hydroxide, and 11 with new activating agents.  Activation with phosphoric acid is commonly used for lignocellulosic material and at lower temps.  Zinc chloride generates more surface area than phosphoric acid but is used less due to environmental concerns.  Potassium carbonate, in comparison with potassium hydroxide, produces higher yields and a higher surface area for the adsorption of large pollutant mols. such as dyes.  Activating with potassium hydroxide in terms of surface area and efficiency shows better results than sodium hydroxide for various applications.  Also, the comparison of the phys. mixing method and the impregnation method in activation with alkali metals indicates that the activated carbon obtained through phys. mixing had a higher porosity than the activated carbon produced by the impregnation method.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGprxAh8uKHonrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7hoEVOGsRiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXjsFKhuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=34bea0bcf46a03c5f8e9bb26e62eeeec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201205332"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, P.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Capacitive mechanism of oxygen functional groups on carbon surface in supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yitao; Zhang, Yaohui; Li, Xifei; Lv, Zhe; Wang, Xianjie; Liu, Zhiguo; Huang, Xiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Oxygen functional groups are one of the most important subjects in the study of electrochem. properties of carbon materials which not only can change the wettability, cond. and pore size distributions of carbon materials, but also can occur redox reactions.  In the electrode materials of carbon-based supercapacitors, the oxygen functional groups have been widely used to improve the capacitive performance.  In this paper, we systematically analyzed the reasons for the increase of the capacity that promoted by oxygen functional groups in the charge/discharge cycling tests and the mechanism how the pseudocapacitance is provided by the oxygen functional groups in the acid/alk. aq. electrolyte.  In addn., we in more depth discussed the effect of the oxygen functional groups in electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfaVFuoK6riLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lianGmurjmWqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFyjurzE&amp;md5=c304d8a4365835cdb2ecab54f806a332</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C6DT00600K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oraon, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">De Adhikari, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tiwari, S.                 10.1039/C6DT00600K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D45%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D9113-9126%26journal%3DDalton%2BTrans.%26issue%3D22%26author%3DR.%2BOraon%26author%3DA.%2BDe%2BAdhikari%26author%3DS.%2BK.%2BTiwari%26author%3DG.%2BC.%2BNayak%26title%3DNanoclay-based%2Bhierarchical%2Binterconnected%2Bmesoporous%2BCNT%252FPPy%2Belectrode%2Bwith%2Bimproved%2Bspecific%2Bcapacitance%2Bfor%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2Bsupercapacitors%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6DT00600K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facssuschemeng.3c07202&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6DT00600K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoclay-based hierarchical interconnected mesoporous CNT/PPy electrode with improved specific capacitance for high performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oraon, Ramesh; De Adhikari, Amrita; Tiwari, Santosh Kumar; Nayak, Ganesh Chandra</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">45</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9113-9126</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1477-9226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A natural layered clay known as montmorillonite, a lamellar aluminosilicate with ∼1 nm thickness, has attracted intense attention in ongoing research due to its large natural abundance and environmental friendliness.  Endowed with highly active surface sites the nanoclay has been extensively used in various fields viz. catalysis, biosensors etc. even though the role played by nanoclay on energy storage performance has not been elucidated.  In this present work, a series of nanoclay (Closite 30B) based hierarchical open interconnected mesoporous electrode materials for supercapacitors (SCs) has been synthesized in the presence of carbon nanotubes (CNTs) and polypyrrole (PPy) by a facile in situ and ex situ approach.  The role of nanoclay was explored as a dopant and its substantial doping effect exerted on the electrochem. performance towards energy storage was investigated.  A coating of PPy over CNTs and nanoclay was confirmed from FESEM anal. which revealed the genesis of a nanoclay-supported hierarchical interconnected mesoporous framework.  Furthermore, a PPy-coated CNT array in the presence of nanoclay was found to be highly porous with a high sp. surface area without obvious deterioration.  These interconnected structures can contribute to better penetration of electrolyte ions by shortening the path length for rapid transport of ions and electrons even at high rates.  Cyclic voltammetry measurements revealed that nanoclay based in situ composite (CNP) and ex situ composite (CPN) exhibited a max. specific capacitance of 425 F/g and 317 F/g, resp. at a scan rate of 10 mV/s, which is comparatively higher than that of CP (i.e. PPy-coated CNTs) (76.77 F/g).  Similarly, a 273% increase in the specific capacitance of PPy was achieved after nanoclay incorporation in the nanocomposite NP (i.e. PPy-coated nanoclay) as compared to virgin PPy.  These results are in good agreement with the specific capacitance performance by galvanostatic charging-discharging anal. performed at 5 A/g.  It was also found that all the nanocomposite retains about 94% initial specific capacitance even after 2000 consecutive cycles.  Thus, this kind of nanoclay-based hierarchical nanostructured framework is believed to be extremely beneficial for SCs applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFc74OsuZtwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lianGmurjmWqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xnslamt74%253D&amp;md5=93b113bb2df88f09b880286561827d8c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoms.2021.01.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced carbon materials with different spatial dimensions for supercapacitors</span>. <i>Nano Mater.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced carbon materials with different spatial dimensions for supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xiaoliang; Liu, Ruonan; Zhao, Jing; Fan, Zhuangjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Materials Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Supercapacitors (SCs) have attracted extensive attention due to their ultrahigh power d., fast charging/discharging rate, excellent electrochem. stability and environmental friendliness.  Currently, the main com. electrode materials for SCs are carbon materials in term of low cost, excellent cond., large sp. surface area and good electrochem. stability.  Recently, various dimensional carbon materials including zero dimensional (0D) carbon materials (nanosphere, dot etc.), 1D carbon materials (nanotube, nanofiber etc.), 2D carbon materials (nanosheet) as well as 3D carbon materials have been developed for SCs.  Carbon materials with different spatial dimensions have their unique properties when used as the electrode materials for SCs.  In this review, recent advances in the fabrication of different dimensional carbons for SCs are summarized.  Several key issues for enhancing the electrochem. properties of carbon-based SCs and some mutual relationships among various influence parameters are reviewed, and challenges and perspectives in this field are also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEQzonbwZogbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lianGmurjmWqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXit12ms7fN&amp;md5=18fa791c0a1073495692d9528fe63266</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1088/0957-4484/27/36/365708"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gross, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barragán, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The large-scale prodn. of graphene and reduced-graphene oxide (rGO) requires low-cost and eco-friendly synthesis methods. Temp.-dependent cond. reveals a semiconductor transport behavior, described by the Mott three-dimensional variable range hopping mechanism.  From the localization length, we est. a band-gap value of 0.22(2) eV for an oxygen content of 5%. After optimizing the amt. of KOH, the resulting ST-derived activated carbon prepd. with a KOH to PC-ST mass ratio of 2 (ACST-2) contained 17.04 wt% oxygen and had a large surface area of 1206.85 m2 g-1, which could be attributed to the large no. of micropores in ACST-2. Herein, a facile and cost-effective strategy to design yolk-shell structured trimanganese tetraoxide nanospheres (Mn3O4 NSs) with a distinctive core-void-shell configuration to use as an efficient pos. electrode material in asym. Specifically, the yolk-shell structured Mn3O4 NSs were prepd. by the inclusion of H2O droplets to the Mn precursor-iso-Pr alc. system, which facilitates the inside-out Ostwald ripening process to construct a yolk-shell configuration with porous properties.  In aq. electrolyte soln., the corresponding material exhibited a high specific capacitance (211.36 F g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1), a good rate capability (79.4% at 10 A g-1) and an excellent cycling stability (92% after 2000 cycles) compared to its solid counterparts.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun biomass based carbon nanofibers as high-performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Qiping; Zhang, Yingchao; Chen, Jiaai; Zhu, Mengni; Yang, Chao; Guo, Haoyu; Song, Yueyan; Li, Yao; Zhou, Jinghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial Crops and Products</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">148</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">112181</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The morphol. collapse of pure biomass-based carbon nanofibers (CNFs) is due to the poor thermal stability of cellulose.  Inspired by nature, cellulose and lignin are linked by covalent-bonds in trees made wood extensible and stable.  In this work, an effective strategy was presented to mimic this biol. structure for the prepn. of biomass-based CNFs.  Epichlorohydrin (ECH) is used to form the covalent-bonds between lignin and cellulose-acetate (CA) for a novel precursor material.  With the introduction of covalent-bonds, precursor materials not only exhibit the spinnability of cellulose, but also possess the thermal stability of lignin.  After carbonization, the pure biomass-based CNFs are successfully prepd. and exhibit independent filamentous morphol., uniform diam., large surface area, and power storage capacity.  The specific capacitance of 320.3 F/g is obtained by using the CNFs-6 (prepd. with 10% ECH content) as super-capacitor.  Simultaneously, the biomass-based CNFs super-capacitor device delivers a high energy d. of 30.2 Wh/ kg at the power d. of 400 W/kg.  These results indicate that the introduction of covalent-bonds can effectively increase the energy storage properties significantly.  This novel strategy showed a successful route for the prepn. of high quality and low cost biomass-based CNFs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-KTBC6OeNw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKt3LTe7plKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXksFKqtro%253D&amp;md5=1e285e1769ce754c5128b8056c8d57cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.3390/nano12203630"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thomas, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sain, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oksman, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sustainable Carbon Derived from Sulfur-Free Lignins for Functional Electrical and Electrochemical Devices</span>. <i>Nanomaterials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">20</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3630</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sustainable Carbon Derived from Sulfur-Free Lignins for Functional Electrical and Electrochemical Devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thomas, Bony; Sain, Mohini; Oksman, Kristiina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanomaterials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3630</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOKO</span>;
