        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tech. lignins, kraft, soda, lignoboost, and hydrolysis lignins were used for the prodn. of carbon particles at different carbonization temps., 1000°C and 1400°C.  The results showed that the lignin source and carbonization temp. significantly influenced the carbon quality and microstructure of the carbon particles.  Soda lignin carbonized up to 1400°C showed higher degree of graphitization and exhibited the highest elec. cond. of 335 S·m-1, which makes it suitable for applications, such as electromagnetic interference shielding and conductive composite based structural energy storage devices.  The obtained carbon particles also showed high surface area and hierarchical pore structure.  Kraft lignin carbonized up to 1400°C gives the highest BET surface area of 646 m2 g-1, which makes it a good candidate for electrode materials in energy storage applications.  The energy storage application has been validated in a three-electrode set up device, and a specific capacitance of 97.2 F g-1 was obtained at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 while an energy d. of 1.1 Wh kg-1 was obsd. at a power d. of 50 W kg-1.  These unique characteristics demonstrated the potential of kraft lignin-based carbon particles for electrochem. energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqrkB3XVXt4hbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKt3LTe7plKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XislygsbbE&amp;md5=fc2ea3705ce65c49c6d17c62e159c120</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijbiomac.2023.126271"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of spherical porous carbon from lignin-derived phenolic resin and its application in supercapacitor electrodes</span>. <i>Int.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of spherical porous carbon from lignin-derived phenolic resin and its application in supercapacitor electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Penghui; Yang, Chi; Yi, Dairenjie; Li, Sixian; Wang, Mingkang; Wang, Huan; Jin, Yongcan; Wu, Wenjuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Biological Macromolecules</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">252</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">126271</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IJBMDR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0141-8130</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lignin is the most abundant arom. biomass resource in nature and is the main byproduct of paper industry and biorefinery industry, which has the characteristics of abundant source, renewable and low cost.  Deep eutectic solvents (DES) are a nascent environmentally friendly solvent option that is gaining traction.  DES composed of p-toluenesulfonic acid and choline chloride is used for batch treatment of alk. lignin, and the bio-oil obtained is ternary polymd. with formaldehyde and phenol to obtain lignin phenolic resin.  The porous carbon material is produced through a two-step carbonization process, utilizing phenolic resin derived from lignin as the primary source of carbon.  The morphol. and compn. of the carbon were analyzed by SEM, TEM, XRD, TGA, XPS and Raman spectroscopy, the sp. surface area and pore size distribution were analyzed by BET.  The results showed that the sp. surface area of the lignin-based phenolic resin was significantly higher than that of the pure phenolic resin carbon, and the porous carbon material that was acquired demonstrated a sp. surface area of as much as 1026 m2/g.  In the three-electrode system, the specific capacitance of DLPFC can reach 245.8 F/g (0.25 A/g), with a very small decrease in the value of specific capacitance at 10,000 cycles, with a retention of 97.62% (10 A/g).  The porous carbon demonstrated a specific capacitance of 112.4 F/g at a c.d. of 0.5 A/g, and the capacitance retention rate could still reach 98.8% after 5000 charge/discharge cycles, with high cycling stability (in the two-electrode system).  The prepd. sym. supercapacitors exhibited high energy d. and power d. of 3.9 Wh/kg and 125.0 W/kg.  The results suggest a new idea of high value-added application of lignin phenolic resin for high-performance supercapacitor electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwAYmRpBUwoLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKt3LTe7plKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhslyjurvF&amp;md5=6197520960e955d48917970a5317525b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.indcrop.2022.114689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qing, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of size-controlled all-lignin based carbon nanospheres and their electrochemical performance in supercapacitor</span>. <i>Ind.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of size-controlled all-lignin based carbon nanospheres and their electrochemical performance in supercapacitor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hang; Xiong, Fuquan; Yang, Jiamei; Ma, Bole; Qing, Yan; Chu, Fuxiang; Wu, Yiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial Crops and Products</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lignin, as the second most abundant biomass material in nature, is regarded as an ideal carbon precursor due to the presence of a larger amt. of arom. ring structural unit.  Carbon nanospheres, as one of the vital members of carbon materials, are promising advanced materials for various areas.  However, lignin-based carbon spheres suffered a complex fabrication process, high crosslinking between spheres, and non-adjustable micron size.  Here, all-lignin based carbon nanospheres (LCNS) with tunable size and microstructure were prepd. via self-assembly, stabilization treatment, and carbonization.  Subsequently, their applications in supercapacitor electrode material were investigated.  The results showed that the monodispersed, ordered, and regular carbon nanospheres could be constructed.  The size of LCNS could be tuned ranging from 256 to 416 nm via changing the initial concn. of lignin between 0.5 and 2 mg mL-1.  The as-prepd. LCNS provided a sp. surface area between 652 and 736 m2 g-1 through adjusting the size and microstructure.  When the LCNS was assembled into the electrochem. capacitor, the LCNS electrode materials exhibited a high specific capacitance of 147 F g-1.  Addnl., the LCNS-based sym. capacitor showed an ultralow characteristic relaxation time (0.86 s) and long cycle stability for 10,000 cycles.  The capacitance properties could be regulated via reconciling the size of nanospheres and microstructure induced by carbonization temp.  The governable capacitance performance indicates that the as-prepd. LCNS should be a promising candidate material for energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_sRlE-ufOerVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKt3LTe7plKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1Ont7%252FM&amp;md5=cedd2a9f156e7f83577efcaab44dd1d9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.3389/fmats.2022.859872"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thielke, M.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Application of a novel binder for activated carbon-based electrical double layer capacitors with nonaqueous electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Xianzhong; Zhang, Xiong; Zhang, Haitao; Huang, Bo; Ma, Yanwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Electrochemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we have fabricated activated carbon electrodes using the binder LA135 and assembled elec. double layer capacitors with nonaq. electrolytes of 1 M tetra-Et ammonium tetrafluoroborate (Et4NBF4) in propylene carbonate (PC), 1 M Et4NBF4 in acetonitrile (AN), and 1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium tetrafluoroborate (EMIMBF4) ionic liq., resp.  The main chem. compns. of the binder are polyacrylonitrile and styrene-butadiene rubber.  Scanning electron microscope images show that the conductive agents have been uniformly dispersed on the activated carbons in the electrode.  The thermal stabilities of electrodes using different binders are studied by thermogravimetric anal.  The electrochem. properties of cells in different nonaq. electrolytes are characterized by cyclic voltammetry, electrochem. impedance spectra, galvanostatic charge-discharge, leakage current, and cycle life measurements.  The capacitor in Et4NBF4/AN has the lowest internal resistance and superior high-rate capability, and the one in Et4NBF4/PC has the smallest leakage current.  The capacitor in EMIMBF4 has the energy d. as high as 35.4 Whkg-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 (based on the total mass of active materials), which is 1.6 times higher than that of capacitor in PC electrolyte.  Besides, the electrochem. properties of capacitors with different binders are comparatively studied.  The capacitor using LA135 has the highest specific capacitance and moderate internal resistance comparing with the ones using poly(tetrafluoroethylene), sodium CM-cellulose + styrene-butadiene rubber or poly (vinylidene fluoride).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJNxjkT5sQALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdEmoPeTrcEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXpvV2lsbY%253D&amp;md5=411d2aa132e22239d97291639af5111c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.121906"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oyedotun, K.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison of ionic liquid electrolyte to aqueous electrolytes on carbon nanofibers supercapacitor electrode derived from oxygen-functionalized graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oyedotun, Kabir O.; Masikhwa, Tshifhiwa M.; Lindberg, Simon; Matic, Aleksandar; Johansson, Patrik; Manyala, Ncholu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">375</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facial force-driven reflux technique was used to develop fiber-like carbon material from freeze-dried reduced graphene oxide (RGO) firstly prepd. by using a modified Hummers method.  The carbon nanofibers displayed a high sp. surface area of ∼1317.8 m2 g-1, with good pore size distributions which could be beneficial for energy storage applications.  Electrochem. measurements of the carbon nanofiber electrodes in a sym. configuration with aq. (1 M Na2SO4, 6 M KOH), and protic ionic liq. (1-ethylimidazolium bis(trifluoromethanesulfonly)imide) electrolytes (ILE) displayed excellent electrochem. performance with the dominant elec. double layer capacitor (EDLC) behavior.  The fabricated device shows higher electrochem. performance in the ILE due to its larger cell operating potential (3.0 V) as compared with the aq. electrolytes (0.8 V).  The optimized electrochem. properties esp. in terms of higher specific energy and superior stability, suggest the material's potential applications as electrode for supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAHs1ZFz8xIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdEmoPeTrcEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtF2gu7fE&amp;md5=d03139160da67d4baf11d7fde98b82d2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.01.021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Natarajan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yassar, R.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low temperature carbonization of cellulose nanocrystals for high performance carbon anode of sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Hongli; Shen, Fei; Luo, Wei; Zhu, Shuze; Zhao, Minhua; Natarajan, Bharath; Dai, Jiaqi; Zhou, Lihui; Ji, Xiulei; Yassar, Reza S.; Li, Teng; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">37-44</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cellulose is the most abundant renewable material in nature.  In this work, ordered cellulose nanocrystals (CNCs) have been transformed into porous carbon with an increased short-range ordered lattice and percolated carbon nanofiber at a relatively low carbonization temp. of 1000 °C.  When evaluated as anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the CNC derived porous carbon shows superior performances including a high reversible capacity of 340 mA h/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g, which is one of the highest capacity carbon anodes for SIBs.  Moreover, the rate capability and cycling stability of the porous carbon are also excellent.  The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to the larger interlayer spacing, porous structure, and high elec. cond. arising from the ordered carbon lattice and the percolated carbon nanofiber.  The formation of nano-sized graphitic carbon from the ordered CNC at the low carbonization temp. of 1000 °C is supported by both mol. dynamic simulations and as well as in-situ TEM measurements.  This study shed light on the fundamental understanding of converting hydrocarbon biopolymer from wood to high quality carbon with a large domain of ordered lattice.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQPc2qtZOdgbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdEmoPeTrcEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFaksbs%253D&amp;md5=14cd4f5048c52e02c678282de20d33a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High capacity anode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stevens, D. A.; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. techniques have been used to study the reversible insertion of sodium into hard-carbon host structures at room temp.  In this paper we compare these results with those for lithium insertion in the same materials and demonstrate the presence of similar alkali metal insertion mechanisms in both cases.  Despite the gravimetric capacities being lower for sodium than lithium insertion, we have achieved a reversible sodium capacity of 300 mAh/g, close to that for lithium insertion in graphitic carbon anode materials.  Such materials may therefore be useful as anodes in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpm125w9mEFSbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdEmoPeTrcEQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXisVygtL0%253D&amp;md5=7480ac0a7bc2620ce565b1c21f1e2463</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1149/1.1379565"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D. A.; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2001</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors compare the interactions of lithium and sodium with a range of carbon materials in electrochem. cells.  Through wide angle in situ x-ray scattering studies, both lithium and sodium can be inserted into the interlayer space in disordered carbon materials.  This insertion process is accompanied by an increase in the interlayer spacing in these materials.  Small-angle in situ scattering studies are presented to clearly show the insertion of lithium and sodium into nanopores within disordered hard carbons.  Also very little, if any, sodium can be inserted into graphitic materials in contrast to the large capacity seen for lithium insertion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Microbial electrolysis cells (MECs) are one of the most promising innovation amongst bio-electrochem. systems for biohydrogen prodn.  A wide variety of wastewaters and org. wastes i.e., sodium acetate, glucose, glycerol, domestic wastewater, sugar industries effluent, food processing wastewater, industrial wastewater, etc. can be utilized as substrates in MEC.  The objective of this comprehensive review is to study the effects of reactor configuration, electrode materials, and substrates on the max. hydrogen prodn. rate (HPR) and columbic efficiency (CE) of the MEC system.  The obtained results were summarized based on reactor configuration, substrate concn., electrodes, applied voltage, HPR, and CE.  Despite this significant progress, MEC technol. still requires substantial developments to be recognized as a com. viable technol.  At the end of this review, the most promising future perspectives were also discussed which could be the appealing solns. for various problems assocd. with MEC technol.  This review supports energy engineers and researchers to analyze the performance of various MECs for future assistance in research.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplJmbhmjjbobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgVwuJ5sPxVAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xns1Sltg%253D%253D&amp;md5=f2852e402a51a8ac666930a8342c773f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1063/1.3220701"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Omer, A.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Energy use and environmental impacts: a general review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Omer, Abdeen Mustafa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Renewable and Sustainable Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">053101/1-053101/29</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Globally, buildings are responsible for approx. 40% of the total world annual energy consumption.  Most of this energy is for the provision of lighting, heating, cooling, and air conditioning.  Increasing awareness of the environmental impact of CO2 and NOx emissions and chlorofluorocarbons triggered a renewed interest in environmentally friendly cooling and heating technologies.  Under the 1997 Montreal Protocol, governments agreed to phase out chems. used as refrigerants that have the potential to destroy stratospheric ozone.  It was therefore considered desirable to reduce energy consumption and decrease the rate of depletion of world energy reserves and pollution of the environment.  One way of reducing building energy consumption is to design buildings that are more economical in their use of energy for heating, lighting, cooling, ventilation, and hot water supply.  Passive measures, particularly natural or hybrid ventilation rather than air conditioning, can dramatically reduce primary energy consumption.  However, exploitation of renewable energy in buildings and agricultural greenhouses can also significantly contribute toward reducing dependency on fossil fuels.  Therefore, promoting innovative renewable applications and reinforcing the renewable energy market will contribute to preservation of the ecosystem by reducing emissions at local and global levels.  This will also contribute to the amelioration of environmental conditions by replacing conventional fuels with renewable energies that produce no air pollution or greenhouse gases.  The provision of good indoor environmental quality (IEQ) while achieving energy and cost efficient operation of the heating, ventilating, and air-conditioning plants in buildings represents a multivariant problem.  The comfort of building occupants is dependent on many environmental parameters including air speed, temp., relative humidity, and quality in addn. to lighting and noise.  The overall objective is to provide a high level of building performance, which can be defined as IEQ, energy efficiency (EE), and cost efficiency (CE).  IEQ is the perceived condition of comfort that building occupants experience due to the phys. and psychol. conditions to which they are exposed by their surroundings.  The main phys. parameters affecting IEQ are air speed, temp., relative humidity, and quality.  EE is related to the provision of the desired environmental conditions while consuming the minimal quantity of energy.  CE is the financial expenditure on energy relative to the level of environmental comfort and productivity that the building occupants attained.  The overall CE can be improved by improving the IEQ and the EE of a building.  The increased availability of reliable and efficient energy services stimulates new development alternatives.  Anticipated patterns of future energy use and consequent environmental impacts (acid pptn., ozone depletion, and greenhouse effect or global warming) are comprehensively discussed in this paper.  Throughout the theme several issues relating to renewable energies, environment, and sustainable development are examd. from both current and future perspectives.  It is concluded that renewable environmentally friendly energy must be encouraged, promoted, implemented, and demonstrated by full-scale plant esp. for use in remote rural areas.  (c) 2009 American Institute of Physics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGM-kJmOHwKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjoGSMvf06rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXlslGjsb0%253D&amp;md5=afc115a4f18b37d7ac7ce34b510a3139</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/er.7091"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muddasar, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liaquat, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abdullah, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Khoja, A.                 10.1002/er.7091</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Evaluating the use of unassimilated bio-anode with different exposed surface areas for bioenergy production using solar-powered microbial electrolysis cell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Muddasar, Muhammad; Liaquat, Rabia; Abdullah, Ali; Khoja, Asif Hussain; Shahzad, Nadia; Iqbal, Naseem; Ali, Muhammad Ishtiaq; Uddin, Azhar; Ullah, Sami</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Energy Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">45</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Summary : The microbial electrolysis cell (MEC) is an emerging technol. for bioenergy prodn. using org. wastewater.  Normally, a preassimilated bio-anode is utilized by the MEC to break down the org. content, but the formation and assimilation of microbial community at the anode surface is a time-consuming process.  This study utilized a novel unassimilated Ni-foam anode for the first time in solar-powered MEC for bioenergy prodn.  Synthetic dairy manure wastewater (SDMW) was used both as substrate and an inoculum in the solar-powered tubular MEC.  The impacts of the exposed surface area of the bio-anode on bioenergy prodn. were evaluated by utilizing two different sepn. techniques (rate-limited bio-anode - MEC and fully exposed bio-anode - MEC).  The former technique achieves a max. methane prodn. rate of 30.35 ± 0.03 mL/L, 14.2% more than that achieved by the later mentioned technique (26.4 ± 0.05 mL/L).  Hydrogen prodn. was approx. 800 ± 5 mm3 in both experimentations.  The max. generated current in the rate limited bio-anode - MEC was 35.5 mA.  Scanning electron microscope images confirmed the formation of rod-shaped along with round-shaped microbial communities on the anode surface, and, interestingly, round-shaped bacteria were also grown on the cathode surface.  The bioenergy (H2 and CH4) produced using SDMW within first 13 days of operation, along with the formation of a microbial community, was a significant success in this area and has opened up many research opportunities for producing instant bioenergy from org. waste.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-5RqlsoLb4rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjoGSMvf06rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslWru77P&amp;md5=3b3170f39c2090d16d18e3290a2d64a7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA10504J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Overview of cellulose-based flexible materials for supercapacitors</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">7278</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7300</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D0TA10504J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Overview of cellulose-based flexible materials for supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Zhe; Qu, Keqi; You, Yue; Huang, Zhanhua; Liu, Shouxin; Li, Jian; Hu, Qian; Guo, Zhanhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7278-7300</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To tackle the crisis of fossil energy shortage and global warming, exploring a series of efficient, portable devices for the conversion/storage of clean and renewable energy sources has remained a significant topic.  Supercapacitors as an advanced energy storage device have the properties of portability and stable performance, electrode materials esp. flexible electrode materials as important components of supercapacitors have drawn great attention in various emerging fields such as portable, wearable electronics and memory materials.  Based on high aspect ratios, sp. surface areas, porosity, mech. properties and excellent flexibility, natural polysaccharide cellulose and its derivs. have become promising building polymers for flexible electrode materials.  In view of poor elec. cond. and low areal capacitance, the compd. modification of cellulose flexible materials and the corresponding application in flexible electrodes are reviewed.  To further illustrate their versatile properties and performances, cellulose-based flexible electrolytes and membranes are summarized with detailed examples.  Overall, this review covers recent advances regarding cellulose-based flexible materials for different components including electrodes, electrolytes and membranes used in supercapacitors and expects to provide refs. for further research of this promising material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRr-c1yvTxzrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjoGSMvf06rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXht1SltLw%253D&amp;md5=7a876480de1d3b1088e813df79acda3c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201100984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fulvio, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Carbon materials have attracted intense interests as electrode materials for electrochem. capacitors, because of their high surface area, elec. cond., chem. stability and low cost.  Activated carbons produced by different activation processes from various precursors are the most widely used electrodes.  Recently, with the rapid growth of nanotechnol., nanostructured electrode materials, such as carbon nanotubes and template-synthesized porous carbons have been developed.  Their unique elec. properties and well controlled pore sizes and structures facilitate fast ion and electron transportation.  In order to further improve the power and energy densities of the capacitors, carbon-based composites combining elec. double layer capacitors (EDLC)-capacitance and pseudo-capacitance have been explored.  They show not only enhanced capacitance, but as well good cyclability.  Recent progress on carbon-based electrode materials is summarized, including activated carbons, carbon nanotubes, and template-synthesized porous carbons, in particular mesoporous carbons.  Their advantages and disadvantages as electrochem. capacitors are discussed.  The future trends of electrochem. capacitors with high energy and power are proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbtLKCSuKRLLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjoGSMvf06rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1Wrs7jE&amp;md5=90635c29d366318b663e22827b54f043</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12538"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">She, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Natural Lignin: A Sustainable and Cost-Effective Electrode Material for High-Temperature Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Waste engine oil is a toxic and hazardous waste; it is estd. that about 45 million tons of waste engine oil are generated per yr worldwide.  Herein, waste engine oil was first recycled as a raw material to fabricate hierarchical porous carbon nanosheets. Cellulose, an abundant natural polymer, has promising potential to be used for energy storage systems because of its excellent mech., structural, and phys. characteristics.  This review discusses the structural features of cellulose and describes its potential application as an electrode, separator, and binder, in various types of high-performing batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports the effects of activation temps. on the porous development and electrochem. performance of activated carbons.  Herein, activated carbons were prepd. from the biowaste of mangosteen peel by using KOH activation at temps. of 400, 600, and 800°C.  The results demonstrate that the sp. surface area increases with increasing the activation temps. in which the well-developed porous structure after KOH activation at 800°C provides the highest sp. surface area of 1039 m2 g-1.  At 600°C, the activated carbon delivers the highest specific capacitance value of 182 F g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 in 3 M KOH aq. electrolyte.  This is correlated well with its high micropore fractions (99%).  Moreover, it was found that the activation temp. changes the major contribution of oxygen-contg. functional group on surface of activated carbon, which is beneficial for the enhancement of the specific capacitance value of activated carbon at the temp. of 600°C.  This work suggests that the activation temp. is a key to optimizing the electrochem. performance of activated carbons.  Overall, our activated carbons can be considered as a strong candidate for use as electrode materials in supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqVhtnf-BNWBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjUXZfLedvJw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xis1aiurfM&amp;md5=8852d7a47dec4633b5760de938075092</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.materresbull.2021.111281"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bamboo-derived porous carbons for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span>. <i>Mater. The as-prepd. BC-CNa owns proper N, O co-doping, diverse carbon defects, and high sp. surface area and pore vol.  Owing to the combined effect of these features, the ZnHS fabricated with this BC-CNa as the cathode material exhibits much higher specific capacities and energy densities than the ZnHSs based on pristine bamboo-derived carbon (BC), bamboo plus C4H6N2 derived carbon (BC-C), and bamboo plus NaNO3 derived carbon (BC-Na).  The max. specific capacity and energy d. of BC-CNa based ZnHS can reach 51.4 mA h g-1 and 48.3 Wh kg-1, resp.  And this ZnHS also exhibits superb cycle stability with 96% capacity retention after 90,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrw-mVbkSigrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjUXZfLedvJw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXls1SkurY%253D&amp;md5=37e22e3bb2a7b62ca73c098ec80c61c4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2023.04.112"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cross-linking and self-assembly synthesis of tannin-based carbon frameworks cathode for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crosslinking and self-assembly synthesis of tannin-based carbon frameworks cathode for Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Shuxin; Wei, Qinhong; Fan, Huailin; Zhang, Yuanrong; Gao, Guoming; Hu, Xun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon frameworks with well-developed porosity present broad application prospects in energy-related materials, and green prepn. still face challenges.  Herein, the tannins-derived framework-like carbon material is obtained by crosslinking and self-assembly strategy.  The phenolic hydroxyl and quinones in tannin crosslinking react with the amine groups in the methenamine by simple stirring, which drives the self-assembly of tannins and methenamine, contributing to the reaction products being pptd. in soln. as aggregates with framework-like structure.  The porosity and micromorphol. of framework-like structures are further enriched by the thermal stability difference between tannin and methenamine.  The methenamine of framework-like structures is entirely removed by the sublimation and decompn. and the tannin is transformed into carbon materials inheriting framework-like structures after the carbonization, which offers the path for rapid electron transport.  The framework-like structure, excellent sp. surface area and nitrogen doping give the assembled Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors a superior specific capacitance of 165.3 mAh·g-1 (350.4 F·g-1).  This device could be charged to 1.87 V to power the bulb by using solar panels.  This study proves that the tannin-derived framework-like carbon is a promising electrode of the Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors, which is beneficial for value-added and industrial supercapacitors application of green feedstocks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPv9X1LPo4PrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjUXZfLedvJw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost, high-performance, and long-life cathode materials are highly desired for zinc ion hybrid supercapacitors (ZHSs).  Here, an N, O co-doped two-dimensional (2D) carbon nanosheet material is successfully fabricated via a one-step combustion conversion of wood for the excellent usage as the cathode material in zinc-ion hybrid supercapacitors.  This novel combustion conversion synthesis with Zn(NO3)2·6H2O as oxidizer and urea as fuel can easily achieve the carbonization, pore-forming, and heteroatom doping within a one-step process.  More interestingly, the resulting N, O co-doped porous carbon owns relatively uniform 2D sheet structure and very high sp. surface area (1248 m2 g-1), which can not only provide short elec./ionic transfer path plus optimized wettability and cond. for high power output, but also offer abundant interfacial active sites as well as improved ion adsorption capacity for high energy storage.  Benefiting from these advantages, the ZHS based on this N, O co-doped 2D carbon nanosheets exhibits a superior specific capacity of 111.0 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, high rate capability of 57.6% capacity retention at a 30-fold higher current, and attractive energy d. of 109.5 Wh kg-1 at 225 W kg-1.  More gratifyingly, it displays ultralong cycling life with 92.7% capacity reservation after 50,000 charge and discharge cycles.  Moreover, a quasi-solid ZHS with N, O co-doped 2D carbon nanosheets coated on the carbon cloth as the cathode also displays satisfactory specific capacity (34.6 mAh g-1), impressive energy d. (27.7 Wh kg-1), and nice flexibility.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFItdrbJNRErVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjUXZfLedvJw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1ekur3F&amp;md5=6fca247c3e0177f072a6dce23a2f6db0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1016/B978-0-12-823702-1.00011-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing sustainable and efficient thermoelec. materials is a challenge because the most common thermoelec. materials are based on rare elements such as bismuth and telluride.  In this context, we have produced bio-based carbon nanofibres (CNFs) derived from mixts. of polyacrylonitrile and lignin using electrospinning.  The addn. of lignin (up to 70%) reduces the diam. of CNFs from 450 nm to 250 nm, increases sample flexibility, and promotes inter-fiber fusion.  The cryst. structure of the CNFs was analyzed by Raman spectroscopy.  The elec. cond. and the Seebeck coeff. were evaluated as function of the lignin content in the precursor and carbonised equiv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lignin, one of the renewable constituents in natural plant biomasses, holds great potential as a sustainable source of functional carbon materials.  Tremendous research efforts have been made on lignin-derived carbon electrodes for rechargeable batteries.  However, lignin is considered as one of the most promising carbon precursors for the development of high-performance, low-cost porous carbon electrode materials for supercapacitor applications. This review, therefore, offers a basis for the utilization of lignin as a pivotal precursor for the synthesis of porous carbons for use in supercapacitor electrode applications.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrode and electrolyte materials with higher performance, longer life, and lower cost need to be developed, given the substantial growing demand for advanced electrochem. energy systems.  Lignin, the second most abundant natural polymer, has been successfully demonstrated to be a viable precursor or feedstock for the prepn. of high-performance electrochem. energy materials and components such as electrodes, electrolyte additives, membrane separators, and binders.  Moreover, techno-economic analyses indicate that it is possible to prep. cost-effective carbon structures from lignin at engineering scale, in contrast with current carbon products.  These facts suggest that the scalable conversion of lignin into high-value energy materials will offer a promising pathway to not only promote the utilization and valorization of lignin but also boost the development of advanced electrochem. energy systems.  This review examines cutting-edge renewable energy materials derived from various lignin compds. and their applications in electrochem. energy systems with an emphasis on supercapacitors, rechargeable batteries, and fuel cells.  Meanwhile, this review also aims to carve out the crit. barriers for lignin-derived high-performance materials for energy applications, and to identify viable approaches for the synthesis of sustainable new energy materials. © 2020 Society of Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This study aims at demonstrating that wastes from anaerobic biodigester plants can be effectively valorized as functional materials to be implemented in technologies that enable efficient energy management and water treatment, therefore simultaneously addressing the Water-Energy-Waste Nexus challenges.  Lignin, the main solid residue of the biodigester plant, has been valorized into activated biochar with a mild activation agent, like KHCO3, to produce electrode of supercapacitors and microbial fuel cells.  In addn., the same sludge that is the liq. effluent of the biodigester plant has been exploited as inoculum and electrolyte for the MFC.  The lignin-derived carbons obtained at lignin/KHCO3 mass ratios of 1:0.5 (LAC-0.5) and 1:2 (LAC-2) comprised of mesopores and micropores displaying BETs of 1558 m2g-1 and 1879 m2g-1, resp.  LAC-2 carbon exhibited a superior specific capacitance of 114 F g-1 in 2.5 M KNO3 with respect to LAC-0.5.  A supercapacitor with LAC-2 electrodes was built displaying specific energy specific power up to 10 Wh kg-1 and 6.9 kW kg-1, resp.  Durability tests showed that the device was able to maintain a capacitance retention of 84.5% after 15,000 charge-discharge cycles.  The lignin-derived carbons were also studied as electrocatalysts for ORR in a neutral medium.  The LAC-2 showed higher ORR electrocatalytic activity than LAC-0.5.  The interconnected porous network and the high surface area made the lignin-derived porous carbons suitable electrode materials for dual applications.  The feasibility of the use of LAC 2 carbon incorporated in an air breathing cathode for MFC applications is also reported.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDvzWmLCPef7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQxzSIhubgTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslWltLbJ&amp;md5=242e1d507b8fbdc0a7b8ec848a47ea49</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijbiomac.2022.09.097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Beaucamp, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muddasar, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Crawford, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Collins, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchically porous carbon aerogels (CAs) were synthesized by following a green, facile prepn. route involving ice-templating and lyophilization followed by carbonization.  For the first time, we report CAs prepd. with a cooling rate of 7.5 K/min, demonstrating a very high sp. surface area (SSA) of 1260 m2 g-1 without any phys. or chem. activation steps, and the electrode prepd. using the latter aerogel showed superior electrochem. performance with a specific capacitance of 410 F g-1 at 2 m V s-1 with a cyclic stability of 94% after 4500 charge-discharge cycles. The ice-templating process and the cooling rate were found to have a large effect on the generation of the nanoporous structure and the sp. surface area of carbon aerogels, while the solid content of the lignin-nanocellulose suspension showed negligible effects.  When assembled as a supercapacitor (SC), a remarkable specific capacitance of 240 F g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 was achieved.  The relaxation time const. for the prepd. SC was 1.3 s, which shows the fast response of these SCs.  In addn., an energy d. of 4.3 Wh kg-1 was also obtained at a power d. of 500 W kg-1. Compared with dry KOH activation agent, the wet KOH shows exfoliation effect on assisting the formation of hierarchical porous structure of LHPC.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Understanding the thermal behavior of lignin is crucial to realize its valorization as an engineering polymer.  Two hardwood lignins, organosolv (OSL) and chem. modified kraft lignin (ML) were chosen to represent important classes of renewable and abundant raw materials.  The relation between ionic mobility and viscosity in OSL and ML was studied.  The rheol. results were interpreted in terms of the competitive processes of thermal plasticization and stiffening through crosslinking.  Results show that with OSL, crosslinking proceeds relatively rapidly, and this is consistent with its more reactive structure.  Higher mol. wt. (Mw) influenced the melt stability as crosslinking kinetics was reduced and this was attributed to the redn. of chain ends available for crosslinking reactions.  Scanning calorimetry has shown that both materials are glassy and pass through the glass transition between 100 °C and 115 °C, with the higher mol. wt. modified material having a slightly higher Tg.  Both lignins show pronounced maxima in the Gram-Schmidt plots for methane or methanol around 400 °C.  However, a significant difference between the materials is obsd. with the detection of a strong carbonyl peak in the evolution products of the ML, which is attributed to the scission of the hydroxypropyl substituent present in the ML structure.  The differences in the degrdn. processes are further reflected in the dielec. properties of the partially degraded materials where loss maxima occur at different temps. and show different degrees of frequency dependence.  An important observation is the difference in cond., where higher values for OSL are attributed to the crosslinking between adjacent benzene rings, whereas with the ML, a lower cond. is assocd. with intrinsically less conductive intermol. linkages.  These results demonstrate that the thermal decompn. of the two lignins follows significantly different paths at the mol. level.  With the more reactive OSL, it appears to be the case that there is a greater tendency to form direct ring to ring crosslinks and this is significant for the properties of the intended end product.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq3ub32NUTw4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljJ_1JmfNd9pg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlajsbrI&amp;md5=f5f8e66e7cc1de8b4190bec0844c5e89</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201907176"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hanaor, D. Freeze casting, also known as ice templating, is a particularly versatile technique that has been applied extensively for the fabrication of well-controlled biomimetic porous materials based on ceramics, metals, polymers, biomacromols., and carbon nanomaterials, endowing them with novel properties and broadening their applicability.  The principles of different directional freeze-casting processes are described and the relationships between processing and structure are examd.  Recent progress in freeze-casting assisted assembly of low dimensional building blocks, including graphene and carbon nanotubes, into tailored micro- and macrostructures is then summarized.  Emerging trends relating to novel materials as building blocks and novel freeze-cast geometries-beads, fibers, films, complex macrostructures, and nacre-mimetic composites-are presented.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon materials are often used as both pos. and neg. electrodes (bipolar electrode materials) in energy storage devices, which significantly reduces the prepn. complexity of the electrode.  Herein, oxygen-modified carbon nanotubes mounted on carbon cloth (CCC) present a high areal capacitance as both pos. and neg. electrodes in a safe neutral electrolyte.  The introduction of oxygen functional groups facilitates the formation of many electrochem. active sites and defects conducive to ion diffusion.  When carbon materials are utilized as neg. electrodes, the charge storage characteristics are mainly dependent on the adsorption and desorption of the ions (corresponding to the elec. double layer capacitance).  Whereas, when utilized as pos. electrodes, the charge storage characteristics come from the intercalation and de-intercalation of the electrolyte ions in the multi-defect carbon material.  The max. areal capacitance measured at the pos. electrode and neg. electrode was 336 mF cm-2 and 158 mF cm-2, resp.  The measured areal capacitance of the assembled sym. supercapacitors was 93.6 mF cm-2, and the areal energy d. reached 33μW h cm-2 at a power d. of 793μW cm-2. Herein, the prepn. of carbon nanofibres from biopolymer blends of lignin (byproduct from the paper and pulp industry) and polylactic acid (PLA) or a thermoplastic elastomeric polyurethane (TPU) is described.  SEM anal. shows the evolving microstructural morphol. after each processing step (electrospinning, stabilization and carbonisation).  Importantly, it is possible to tailor the nanofibre porosity by utilizing miscibility/immiscibility rules between lignin and the polymer additive (PLA/TPU).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Conventional soft template methods for the synthesis of ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs) use unsustainable, toxic and carcinogenic phenolic compds. as carbon precursors and aldehydes as crosslinkers.  Lignin is a potential carbon precursor for OMC prodn., but its direct use as a carbon precursor has not been possible.  Herein, a protocol is developed for the direct one-pot synthesis of OMCs using lignin from agricultural waste sources (walnut shell, macadamia nut shell, and tobacco stem) as a sole carbon precursor through coordinated interactions between lignin functional groups and metal ligands via classical solvent evapn. induced self-assembly (EISA).  The protocol is demonstrated for the one-pot synthesis of metal oxide- or elemental metal-linked OMCs (defined as M#OMCs) using many different metal ions (Ni2+, Mg2+, Fe3+, Co2+, Zn2+, La3+, and Ce3+) that form well-ordered mesoporous structures having uniform metal dispersion.  As one application, Ni#OMC is shown to effectively catalyze biomass hydrogenation, transfer hydrogenation and isomerization reactions.  The protocol developed for OMC materials from lignin is expected to have wide applications in catalysis, adsorption, sensor, drug delivery and energy storage fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohJbWsKtNIZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPsZjdqZvGVg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Activated carbon refers to a wide range of carbonised materials of high degree of porosity and high surface area.  Activated carbon has many applications in the environment and industry for the removal, retrieval, sepn. and modification of various compds. in liq. and gas phases.  Selection of the chem. activator agent is a major step controlling the performance and applicability of activated carbon.  Here, we review chem. activators used to produce activated carbon.  We compare the impregnation method with the phys. mixing method used in activating with alkali hydroxides.  We selected 81 articles from Google Scholar, PubMed, Scopus, Science Direct, Embase and Medlin databases.  Eighteen articles report the activation with potassium hydroxide, 17 with phosphoric acid, 15 with zinc chloride, 11 with potassium carbonate, nine with sodium hydroxide, and 11 with new activating agents.  Activation with phosphoric acid is commonly used for lignocellulosic material and at lower temps.  Zinc chloride generates more surface area than phosphoric acid but is used less due to environmental concerns.  Potassium carbonate, in comparison with potassium hydroxide, produces higher yields and a higher surface area for the adsorption of large pollutant mols. such as dyes.  Activating with potassium hydroxide in terms of surface area and efficiency shows better results than sodium hydroxide for various applications.  Also, the comparison of the phys. mixing method and the impregnation method in activation with alkali metals indicates that the activated carbon obtained through phys. mixing had a higher porosity than the activated carbon produced by the impregnation method.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGprxAh8uKHonrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPsZjdqZvGVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXjsFKhuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=34bea0bcf46a03c5f8e9bb26e62eeeec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201205332"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Oxygen functional groups are one of the most important subjects in the study of electrochem. properties of carbon materials which not only can change the wettability, cond. and pore size distributions of carbon materials, but also can occur redox reactions.  In the electrode materials of carbon-based supercapacitors, the oxygen functional groups have been widely used to improve the capacitive performance.  In this paper, we systematically analyzed the reasons for the increase of the capacity that promoted by oxygen functional groups in the charge/discharge cycling tests and the mechanism how the pseudocapacitance is provided by the oxygen functional groups in the acid/alk. aq. electrolyte.  In addn., we in more depth discussed the effect of the oxygen functional groups in electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfaVFuoK6riLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPsZjdqZvGVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFyjurzE&amp;md5=c304d8a4365835cdb2ecab54f806a332</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C6DT00600K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oraon, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">De Adhikari, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tiwari, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A natural layered clay known as montmorillonite, a lamellar aluminosilicate with ∼1 nm thickness, has attracted intense attention in ongoing research due to its large natural abundance and environmental friendliness.  Endowed with highly active surface sites the nanoclay has been extensively used in various fields viz. catalysis, biosensors etc. even though the role played by nanoclay on energy storage performance has not been elucidated.  In this present work, a series of nanoclay (Closite 30B) based hierarchical open interconnected mesoporous electrode materials for supercapacitors (SCs) has been synthesized in the presence of carbon nanotubes (CNTs) and polypyrrole (PPy) by a facile in situ and ex situ approach.  The role of nanoclay was explored as a dopant and its substantial doping effect exerted on the electrochem. performance towards energy storage was investigated.  A coating of PPy over CNTs and nanoclay was confirmed from FESEM anal. which revealed the genesis of a nanoclay-supported hierarchical interconnected mesoporous framework.  Furthermore, a PPy-coated CNT array in the presence of nanoclay was found to be highly porous with a high sp. surface area without obvious deterioration.  These interconnected structures can contribute to better penetration of electrolyte ions by shortening the path length for rapid transport of ions and electrons even at high rates.  Cyclic voltammetry measurements revealed that nanoclay based in situ composite (CNP) and ex situ composite (CPN) exhibited a max. specific capacitance of 425 F/g and 317 F/g, resp. at a scan rate of 10 mV/s, which is comparatively higher than that of CP (i.e. PPy-coated CNTs) (76.77 F/g).  Similarly, a 273% increase in the specific capacitance of PPy was achieved after nanoclay incorporation in the nanocomposite NP (i.e. PPy-coated nanoclay) as compared to virgin PPy.  These results are in good agreement with the specific capacitance performance by galvanostatic charging-discharging anal. performed at 5 A/g.  It was also found that all the nanocomposite retains about 94% initial specific capacitance even after 2000 consecutive cycles.  Thus, this kind of nanoclay-based hierarchical nanostructured framework is believed to be extremely beneficial for SCs applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFc74OsuZtwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljhV9BZLW1nZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xnslamt74%253D&amp;md5=93b113bb2df88f09b880286561827d8c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoms.2021.01.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced carbon materials with different spatial dimensions for supercapacitors</span>. <i>Nano Mater.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The morphol. collapse of pure biomass-based carbon nanofibers (CNFs) is due to the poor thermal stability of cellulose.  Inspired by nature, cellulose and lignin are linked by covalent-bonds in trees made wood extensible and stable.  In this work, an effective strategy was presented to mimic this biol. structure for the prepn. of biomass-based CNFs.  Epichlorohydrin (ECH) is used to form the covalent-bonds between lignin and cellulose-acetate (CA) for a novel precursor material.  With the introduction of covalent-bonds, precursor materials not only exhibit the spinnability of cellulose, but also possess the thermal stability of lignin.  After carbonization, the pure biomass-based CNFs are successfully prepd. and exhibit independent filamentous morphol., uniform diam., large surface area, and power storage capacity.  The specific capacitance of 320.3 F/g is obtained by using the CNFs-6 (prepd. with 10% ECH content) as super-capacitor.  Simultaneously, the biomass-based CNFs super-capacitor device delivers a high energy d. of 30.2 Wh/ kg at the power d. of 400 W/kg.  These results indicate that the introduction of covalent-bonds can effectively increase the energy storage properties significantly.  This novel strategy showed a successful route for the prepn. of high quality and low cost biomass-based CNFs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-KTBC6OeNw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwKI9edc7tBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXksFKqtro%253D&amp;md5=1e285e1769ce754c5128b8056c8d57cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.3390/nano12203630"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thomas, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sain, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oksman, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sustainable Carbon Derived from Sulfur-Free Lignins for Functional Electrical and Electrochemical Devices</span>. <i>Nanomaterials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">20</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3630</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of spherical porous carbon from lignin-derived phenolic resin and its application in supercapacitor electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Penghui; Yang, Chi; Yi, Dairenjie; Li, Sixian; Wang, Mingkang; Wang, Huan; Jin, Yongcan; Wu, Wenjuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Biological Macromolecules</span>
